<div id="descriptionContainer">
      <div style="right:0" class="readable stacked" id="description">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer107444400737851482">In the deft hands of Neil Gaiman, magic is no mere illusion . . . and anything is possible. In <em>Smoke and Mirrors</em>, Gaiman's imagination and supreme artistry transform a mundane world into a place of terrible wonders—where an old woman can purchase the Holy Grail at a thrift store, where assassins advertise their services in the Yellow Pages under "Pest Control," and where a</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText107444400737851482">In the deft hands of Neil Gaiman, magic is no mere illusion . . . and anything is possible. In <em>Smoke and Mirrors</em>, Gaiman's imagination and supreme artistry transform a mundane world into a place of terrible wonders—where an old woman can purchase the Holy Grail at a thrift store, where assassins advertise their services in the Yellow Pages under "Pest Control," and where a frightened young boy must barter for his life with a mean-spirited troll living beneath a bridge by the railroad tracks. Explore a new reality, obscured by smoke and darkness yet brilliantly tangible, in this extraordinary collection of short works by a master prestidigitator. It will dazzle your senses, touch your heart, and haunt your dreams.<br /><br />Contents <br />ix • Reading the Entrails: A Rondel • (1997) • poem by Neil Gaiman<br />1 • An Introduction (Smoke and     <div class="section firstReview">
      

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_38777647">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/38777647" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/1033675-matt" class="left imgcol" title="Matt"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1325271531p2/1033675.jpg" alt="Matt" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/38777647?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Dec 30, 2008</a>

      <a href="/user/show/1033675-matt" class="user" title="Matt">Matt</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/16790.Smoke_and_Mirrors" title="Paperback 9780380789023" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer38777647">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8256928336795887977">'Smoke and Mirrors' is the first of two short story collections written by Neil Gaiman. This title was first published in 1998, while 'Fragile Things' came out in 2006. Having read 'Fragile Things' mere months ago I was doing quite a bit of comparison between the two as I worked my way through 'Smoke and Mirrors'. While there are a lot of similarities between the two, there are also many differences.<br /><br />Both collections involve Gaiman doing what he does best, that is taking our own myths, fables, an</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText8256928336795887977">'Smoke and Mirrors' is the first of two short story collections written by Neil Gaiman. This title was first published in 1998, while 'Fragile Things' came out in 2006. Having read 'Fragile Things' mere months ago I was doing quite a bit of comparison between the two as I worked my way through 'Smoke and Mirrors'. While there are a lot of similarities between the two, there are also many differences.<br /><br />Both collections involve Gaiman doing what he does best, that is taking our own myths, fables, and folklore, tweaking them to better resonate with our modern culture, and handing them back to us complete with the grit and gristle that were absent from the versions that we received as children. While this seems to be an over-arching theme to most of the stories in 'Fragile Things', it still shows up occasionally in 'Smoke and Mirrors' along with so much else. <br /><br />Gaiman takes the reader to so many places throughout these stories. These include a couple of nods to writers that surely influenced him along the way (Lovecraft and Moorcock, specifically), a writer struggling through a screenplay that has been watered down by the movie studio discovering the legendary Hollywood of old, and political intrigue amongst the angels in heaven. Lawrence Talbot also makes an appearance in a tale involving the Wolf Man. Gaiman's books are usually shelved in the Sci-Fi/Fantasy section at the average bookstore, which I think is a bit of a disservice as these stories are so much more diverse than the typical view of the Fantasy genre that involves touchy-feely knights riding around on horses and tends to prejudice the typical reader to that genre negatively.<br /><br />A tip to any readers who are in the habit of skipping book introductions: Gaiman actually hides a story within the introduction of this book as a payoff to those who religiously read the introduction. That sort of cleverness suckers me in every time.<br /><br />It may be unwise to compare the stories in 'Smoke and Mirrors' to each other and to 'Fragile Things' as both books represent more of a compilation of Gaiman stories that appeared in other publications over a particular period of his writing career versus something that was put together as an intentional, unified collection. However, as it is great fun to wildly speculate, I believe that the stories in 'Smoke and Mirrors' are bolder than the ones in the later collection. As most of these stories were written around the time that 'Sandman' was finishing its run, I'm wondering if the reason for this was to prove to any naysayers that Gaiman was a serious writer and not just "that comic book guy."<br /><br />These stories may not be something that would be discussed in a college level literature class with the austere professor that lives and dies by the canon, but I don't think that is Gaiman's intention as a writer. He comes from the storyteller tradition, and I feel that such a thing is just as important in feeding one's imagination and intellect as the heavy literature now and again. </span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="8256928336795887977">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <a href="/user/show/1038815-jc" class="left imgcol" title="Jc"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1321228818p2/1038815.jpg" alt="Jc" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/46868996?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jan 01, 2012</a>

      <a href="/user/show/1038815-jc" class="user" title="Jc">Jc</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok">it was ok</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/16790.Smoke_and_Mirrors" title="Paperback 9780380789023" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer46868996">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12125877112218531558">This collection of short works, some not quite complete, is maybe a must read for real Gaiman fans who read everything he does (4 stars for them), but not really for anyone else (only 1 star for the general audience). And I say that as one of those fans. I really like what Gaiman does, both in traditional and graphic novel form, but Smoke and Mirrors is not representative of his best work. Basically, it is a collection of things he never bothered to give a final polish to. Much of S&amp;M is thi</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText12125877112218531558">This collection of short works, some not quite complete, is maybe a must read for real Gaiman fans who read everything he does (4 stars for them), but not really for anyone else (only 1 star for the general audience). And I say that as one of those fans. I really like what Gaiman does, both in traditional and graphic novel form, but Smoke and Mirrors is not representative of his best work. Basically, it is a collection of things he never bothered to give a final polish to. Much of S&amp;M is things that were just workbook exercises, not intended for publication. Some fun ideas, and entertaining for the fan (or for those who want to study how he develops ideas), but others should try American Gods, Anansi Boys, Neverwhere, Good Omens (with T.Pratchett!), or even Coraline or his Sandman graphic novels. It does, however, contain a few real gems for fans. [warning: different editions of the S&amp;M varied the collection slightly, so referring to specific stories may be confusing when discussing the book]</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="12125877112218531558">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1334818531">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3801381302828206518">...Drops of water fell like diamonds from the Angel Lucifer's perfect fingers... From the short story, 'Murder Mysteries'<br />About half way through this volume of short's I was thinking this would probably be a 4 star, maybe a 3.5 actual. Now that I am at the end, having examined the work as a whole, and considering the power of the last 2 stories, I had to rate this a 5. <br />I love the way Neil mixed it up. The collection seemed to be a potpourri of short stories, prose, poetry and lyrical verse. I cou</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText3801381302828206518">...Drops of water fell like diamonds from the Angel Lucifer's perfect fingers... From the short story, 'Murder Mysteries'<br />About half way through this volume of short's I was thinking this would probably be a 4 star, maybe a 3.5 actual. Now that I am at the end, having examined the work as a whole, and considering the power of the last 2 stories, I had to rate this a 5. <br />I love the way Neil mixed it up. The collection seemed to be a potpourri of short stories, prose, poetry and lyrical verse. I could feel his love of mythology, a little touch of H.P. Lovecraft, and another side that I think of as a British Chuck Palahniuk.<br />The last 2 stories, 'Murder Mysteries', and 'Snow, Glass, Apples',made this entire book well worth the read. <br />Murder Mysteries was a unique play on the mythology of God, Lucifer and the angels that I found to be particularly entertaining and thought provoking. Very well done. And Snow, Glass, Apples was also a twist on the old story of Snow White. <br />Neil Gaiman has a style and imagination that makes him one of my favorites. And Smoke and Mirrors reflects his story telling gifts brilliantly. <br /></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="3801381302828206518">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_376488646">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/376488646" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/10478000-april" class="left imgcol" title="April"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1439652786p2/10478000.jpg" alt="April" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/376488646?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jun 22, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/10478000-april" class="user" title="April">April</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/16790.Smoke_and_Mirrors" title="Paperback 9780380789023" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Gaiman fans</span></div>

        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/10478000-april?shelf=fantasy" class="actionLinkLite">fantasy</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/10478000-april?shelf=horror" class="actionLinkLite">horror</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/10478000-april?shelf=short-story-or-stories" class="actionLinkLite">short-story-or-stories</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/10478000-april?shelf=loved" class="actionLinkLite">loved</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer376488646">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3624813321421783366"><em> Bearing in mind I read this on my kindle, so some stories weren't included in the version I read. Also this is hella long.</em><br /><br /><em>All ratings (including notes). * indicates favourite</em><br /><strong>The Wedding Present (Yes, I religiously read introductions):4*</strong><br />In which a picturesque couple are given a quaint wedding present that seems to be a 'retelling' of their coupling; it spins a story of how their marriage could have went wrong. Though this premise may seem outlandish and bizarre, it's terribly relevant and poses</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText3624813321421783366"><em> Bearing in mind I read this on my kindle, so some stories weren't included in the version I read. Also this is hella long.</em><br /><br /><em>All ratings (including notes). * indicates favourite</em><br /><strong>The Wedding Present (Yes, I religiously read introductions):4*</strong><br />In which a picturesque couple are given a quaint wedding present that seems to be a 'retelling' of their coupling; it spins a story of how their marriage could have went wrong. Though this premise may seem outlandish and bizarre, it's terribly relevant and poses significant questions about the lives we choose to live. It's sad to think that some Gaiman fans miss this story;it's precious. <br /><strong>Chivalry:</strong>3.5<br />Quite lovely. The relationship was sweet and Mrs. Whitaker was charming to read. <br /><strong>Nicholas Was...:</strong>4.5<br />An excellent and precisely one hundred word twist on St. Nicholas, aka Santa Claus. Ho ho ho.<br /><strong>The Price:</strong>4<br />Ooh symbolism, symbolism! I adore this story, possibly because I'm so fond of cats. The idea of a knightly cat guardian is wonderful. <br /><strong>Troll Bridge:</strong>3.5<br />I enjoyed this tale, but something lead me to believe that it would be more than it was when it finished, so I wasn't as impressed with the ending. Nevertheless it was immensely thought-provoking and preoccupying. <br /><strong>Don't Ask Jack:</strong>5*<br />Horrifying, afflicting, and downright disturbing. Yep, one of my favourite stories out of the entire book. <br /><strong>The Goldfish Pool and Other Stories:</strong>3<br />I really liked the vintage Hollywood theme but it didn't pull me in. I think I maintained interest simply because it's a quasi-account of personal experience for Gaiman (as he admitted at the start of the book). Riddled with idioms and scathing remarks on Hollywood, it's very entertaining and humorous, but not gripping enough for me.<br /><strong>Eaten (Scenes from a Moving Picture):</strong>3<br />ARGH. I have written on my notepad: 'SEXSEXSEXSEXSEX. GROSSED OUT. NEED SHOWER.'That pretty much summarizes how I feel about this story. ...Bloomin' heteros. <br /><strong>The White Road:</strong>3.5<br />Cool, kind of story you can read over and over again and interpret in many different ways.<br /><strong>Queen Of Knives:</strong>4.5<br />Very alluring; I analysed this to death. I fathomed all sorts of underlying messages and things I could take away. Personally I took this idea of being trapped in a loveless marriage to result in the disappearance. In addition, it's also delectably written. I devoured this story in one bite. <br /><strong>Changes:</strong>4*<br />Exceedingly powerful, especially the end. The mere fact that Rajit (a Scientist) was referring to the people as 'Angels' was of pivotal importance to me. I took away my own meanings for this, some of which I'm certain Gaiman wasn't even attempting to convey. I thought the significance of 'Angels' meant that a conceivably genderless society - or a society in which gender holds no meaning - could be perceived as being that of an angelic, peaceful community. That's just a fraction of what I took away from this, though.<br /><strong>The Daughter of Owls:</strong>2<br />I didn't find this story interesting. The title was inviting but the tale disappointed. I followed everything that happened with little interest as to what <strong>would</strong> eventually happen.<br /><strong>Shoggoth's Old Peculiar:</strong>2<br />Looking back, I don't even remember this story. Needless to say I wasn't that impressed. Beautifully written (as always, oh Gaiman, you wonderful thing) but with little quality for me to recall. I'll duplicate the comment for above: I didn't find this story interesting. The title was inviting but the tale disappointed. I followed everything that happened with little interest as to what <strong>would</strong> eventually happen.<br /><strong>Virus:</strong>3<br />Interesting, cryptic, scary. It reminded me of that short film titled <em>Virus</em> too. <br /><strong>Looking for the Girl:</strong>4/4.5<br />This reminded me a lot of <em>Death in Venice</em> and whilst I didn't have the opportunity to picture a beautiful prepubescent boy walking among the streets of Italy, I still engaged with the divine narrative that retained this sense of beauty never being able to be obtained. I'm also reminded of McConaughey's:<br /><img class="escapedImg" src="http://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380385252r/744118._SX540_SY540_.gif" /><br /><strong>Bay Wolf:</strong>3<br />I'm always captivated by mythical creatures, so I relished this little anecdote (though I don't remember much about it - probably because I was nodding off). <br /><strong>Fifteen Painted Cards from a Vampire Tarot:</strong>5*<br />A collection within a collection: an array of segmented texts that evoke mystery and awe. I loved the relativity toward Tarot cards in particular, especially 'The Fool'. <br /><strong>We Can Get Them for You Wholesale:</strong>4.5*<br />Hilarious and ambiguously intriguing. <em>'They'd been ready for a long time, but they had to be asked.'</em> It reminded me of Vampires having to be granted permission to cross the threshold into our world. <br /><strong>One Life, Furnished in Early Moorcock:</strong>3<br />All I have written down is: 'Something missing, liked the beginning though.' Very informative, April. <br /><strong>Cold Colors:</strong>2.5<br />All I remember is confusion. <br /><strong>The Sweeper of Dreams:</strong>3.5<br />A magical ideal, one that need not be questioned in the unknown and mystical land of dreams. <br /><strong>Foreign Parts:</strong>3.5<br />Excusing the awkward descriptions of symptoms deriving from venereal disease, the alienation of the lower regions of the protagonists body is open to interpretation. The real interest I had was determining whether this was a tale of possession or dispossession<br /><strong>Vampire Sestina:</strong>5*<br />Sensual and delightful, it certainly appealed to my extreme love of Vampiresque material. Kudos to Gaiman also for succeeding in writing quite possibly the toughest form of verse out there.<br /><strong>Mouse:</strong>2<br />Curious but a tale that scurried away pretty easily from my train of thought. <br /><strong>The Sea Change:</strong>4<br />I love the sea and aquatic life in general, therefore I was pretty gripped with this story. I'm also a sucker for mermaids. <br /><strong>When We Went To See The End of The World by Dawnie:Morningside, age 11 1/4:</strong>4<br />This really disturbed me. I don't know why, it just seemed like the complete representation of evil. It maintained the sense of inventive, fictitious evil whilst holding the innocence and relativity of real life. The most blatant representation of this is the mere use of the narration of an 11-year-old. <br /><strong>Desert Wind:</strong>3<br />Nicely told anecdote; it really brings forth the sensation of regret and longing to be somewhere else (which is the reason I read Gaimans books in the first place). I would like to go with the people too. <br /><strong>Tastings:</strong>4.5*<br />Oh, more sexy times. I actually loved the idea of something so frequently deemed emotionless or meaningless in the promiscuity of modern society becoming a personal necessity to someone's character. To be frank, I pried open this story like some sort of literary autopsy and picked apart meanings and interpretations for hours. <br /><strong>Babycakes:</strong>4*<br /><em>'We'll figure something out.'</em> An almost dystopian feel to this, which I always admire. Very haunting and inhuman - yet possible. Foreshadowing the horror of human existence. Superb. <br /><strong>Murder Mysteries:</strong>4<br />I'm not Christian, so forgive me for not fully immersing myself in the retelling of creation or rather Gaiman's 'take' on it. I relished the wholehearted symbolism throughout though. <br /><strong>Snow, Glass and Apples:</strong>3<br />I expected this to be one of my favourites, but sadly it's something that I feel suffered from my high expectations. I originally heard of this in Gaiman's extra in <em>Stardust</em> and thought it was going to be magnificent. It was pretty good, and will forever leave a 'stain' on the Snow White tale for me personally, but truthfully I was expecting more. <br /><br />I originally intended to read one story per night, as it seemed pretty easy to do so; all of the stories are fairly unique and eclectic. However, I was far too engaged to pass up the opportunity to finish the book all at once. I even made notes on each tale after finishing them. <br /><br />Looking back, it’s quite hard to give an overall summary. It’s a wonderful, disturbing, downright peculiar collection of stories that spins you from one adventure to the next weaved in with Gaiman's imaginary genius. Some were decent, others spectacular, few just okay. I frequently sensed some stories were ones that either needed to be developed more, or ones that didn't have enough promise and shouldn't have made it onto the page.<br /><br />Overall rating: <strong>3.5.</strong></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="3624813321421783366">...more</a>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_379644391">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/379644391" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/4159895-petergiaquinta" class="left imgcol" title="Petergiaquinta"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1304003529p2/4159895.jpg" alt="Petergiaquinta" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/379644391?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jun 19, 2013</a>

      <a href="/user/show/4159895-petergiaquinta" class="user" title="Petergiaquinta">Petergiaquinta</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/531127.Smoke_and_Mirrors" title="Hardcover 9780380973644" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer379644391">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12482094750044142696">A guilty pleasure, sure, but with Ray Bradbury's death, I'd suggest that Neil Gaiman is the best storyteller we have today.<br /><br />Consider the words of Harry Bailly (he of the Tabard Inn, not George's brother): "And which of yow that bereth hym best of alle / That is to seyn that telleth in this caas / Tales of best sentence and moost solaas / Shal have a soper at oure aller cost." And I'd buy Gaiman a meal or three for this sundry collection of tales pulled together from over the years and published i</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText12482094750044142696">A guilty pleasure, sure, but with Ray Bradbury's death, I'd suggest that Neil Gaiman is the best storyteller we have today.<br /><br />Consider the words of Harry Bailly (he of the Tabard Inn, not George's brother): "And which of yow that bereth hym best of alle / That is to seyn that telleth in this caas / Tales of best sentence and moost solaas / Shal have a soper at oure aller cost." And I'd buy Gaiman a meal or three for this sundry collection of tales pulled together from over the years and published in <em>Smoke and Mirrors</em>.<br /><br />You might think I'm just showing off with the Middle English, but I don't think it's too much of a stretch to draw parallels between Gaiman and Chaucer. Chaucer's <em>Tales</em> cover a wide range of genres, from the romance to the fabliau to the beast fable to the exemplum and everything in between, and Gaiman uses just as wide a contemporary pallet as Chaucer employed from the Middle Ages. Gaiman moves from the hard-boiled to the horror story; he blends prose and poetry with sci-fi, the sacred and the secular; he has an erotic (?) offering here that transcends mommy porn; heck, he even writes a sestina with vampires in it that works...and that alone has to testify to the genius of the man. Elsewhere Gaiman does everything from the full-blown novel to YA to children's lit; he's written screenplays and comic books, and just about everything he does is golden. Sure he's had some missteps, and not everything in <em>Smoke and Mirrors</em> succeeds at the same level, but hey, the Friar's Tale is a bit dull and the Priest's lengthy sermon is practically unreadable.<br /><br />And like Chaucer (working from Bocaccio and Petrarch and the Thousand and One Nights among other sources), Gaiman is often at his best when he is reworking earlier stories and authors, especially fairy tales and folk tales. His version of Snow White here is a fascinating retelling that's going to stick with me for a long time, and one of my favorites in the book ("Shoggoth's Old Peculiar") grows out of Lovecraft. And even though it's goofy as hell, I even like his pastiche of <em>Beowulf</em> and <em>Baywatch</em> with Larry Talbot thrown in as an added plus.<br /><br />Finally, and thanks for sticking with me this long, Gaiman addresses many of the same concerns Chaucer had: greed and hypocrisy, dreams and where they come from, what makes a good marriage, the role of women in a male-dominated society, and on and on (the intertwining roles of magic and technology in "Cold Colors"? try the Franklin's Tale), but through them all, both authors are really interested in the whole idea of stories and story telling and what makes a good story. And what that is, if you go back to Harry Bailly, is that right blend of "best sentence and moost solaas," and Neil Gaiman just about always gets it right.<br /></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="12482094750044142696">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_34782355">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/34782355" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/140880-latharia" class="left imgcol" title="Latharia"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1182310614p2/140880.jpg" alt="Latharia" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/34782355?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Dec 22, 2008</a>

      <a href="/user/show/140880-latharia" class="user" title="Latharia">Latharia</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>



        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer34782355">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17375806847113495061">Wow. I have to say that just about every story in this collection was highly engaging, and I had strong emotional reactions to several of them, and many "gotcha" type moments. Gaiman is, indeed, a master storyteller. Some of my favorite bits, without giving too much away for those of you who need to add this to your "to read" stack: <br /><br />- the sad workings of Peter's mind in "We Can Get Them For You Wholesale"<br />- the explanation of those who've spurned "The Sweeper of Dreams"<br />- the evolution of perceive</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText17375806847113495061">Wow. I have to say that just about every story in this collection was highly engaging, and I had strong emotional reactions to several of them, and many "gotcha" type moments. Gaiman is, indeed, a master storyteller. Some of my favorite bits, without giving too much away for those of you who need to add this to your "to read" stack: <br /><br />- the sad workings of Peter's mind in "We Can Get Them For You Wholesale"<br />- the explanation of those who've spurned "The Sweeper of Dreams"<br />- the evolution of perceived morality in "Changes"<br />- the mundane conversational aspects of "Tastings"<br />- the story embedded within the story of "Murder Mysteries"<br /><br />I would like to say that this is a wonderful book to have on one's nightstand, to read a short story before bedtime, but I can't say that. Many of the stories (Don't Ask Jack, The White Road, and Snow,Glass,Apples in particular) were downright emotionally disturbing. Good, but disturbing. Don't Ask Jack actually generated a nightmare! *shudder* Great job, Gaiman. *wink*</span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_1840975">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1840975" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/123082-j" class="left imgcol" title="J"><img src="http://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/m_50x66-82093808bca726cb3249a493fbd3bd0f.png" alt="J" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/1840975?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jun 18, 2007</a>

      <a href="/user/show/123082-j" class="user" title="J">J</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok">it was ok</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/16790.Smoke_and_Mirrors" title="Paperback 9780380789023" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Vampires</span></div>

        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1840975">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1078891377189758968">A note: I expect more than I should from this author. I find him to be a brilliant idea man with little substance.<br /><br />-Suggested Reading Order:<br /><br />Murder Mystery<br />Tastings<br />Snow, Glass, Apples <br />Only the End of the World Again<br />Shoggoth’s Old Peculiar <br />We Can Get Them for You Wholesale<br />Chivalry<br />Cold Colors<br />The Price<br /><br />Chivalry- an old woman buys the Holy Grail. A full-armored knight comes to seek the Grail. Cute, long-run and dry. The most wonderful thing about this story is that it is quaint and written as gabbish; a</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText1078891377189758968">A note: I expect more than I should from this author. I find him to be a brilliant idea man with little substance.<br /><br />-Suggested Reading Order:<br /><br />Murder Mystery<br />Tastings<br />Snow, Glass, Apples <br />Only the End of the World Again<br />Shoggoth’s Old Peculiar <br />We Can Get Them for You Wholesale<br />Chivalry<br />Cold Colors<br />The Price<br /><br />Chivalry- an old woman buys the Holy Grail. A full-armored knight comes to seek the Grail. Cute, long-run and dry. The most wonderful thing about this story is that it is quaint and written as gabbish; a runabout talkative form of day-to-day meandering, paying no heed to the extraordinary.<br /><br />Nicholas Was… - my favorite line "Once every year they forced him, sobbing and protesting, into Endless Night." This is a short short story. It seems, in this piece, there was more to be said but wasn’t.<br /><br />The Price- The beginning of this piece is bloody brilliant, reflecting harlequin mythos. The story sidesteps this flight of fancy to anecdote, betraying itself with its narrative<br /><br />Troll Bridge- The strength is the child’s voice (which continues and becomes outlived). The narrative stretches into the mundane: a point and picture of nothingness, an ode to the anticlimactic where, at the end, the story snuffs itself out of hopelessness… like a suicidal cigarette. <br /><br />The White Road- These story-poems were glanced over with some volume of interest. The White Road- could’ve been the premise for the Corpse Bride, except that at the scene where the corpse bride was supposed to get killed, she does not and lives thereafter. <br /><br />Changes- A summary of a man and his time split from an invention- a (not the) cure for cancer, side effect- sex change, and what becomes of it as seen by him. <br /><br />The Daughters of Owls- Phun with mysspellinks. <br /><br />Shoggoth’s Old Peculiar- Gaiman pays homage to H.P. Lovecraft, typing his lines and taking his name. The descriptive presence shows Gaiman's strength as the main character muddles about a town conversing with two drunkards spouting Lovecraft at lengths with lists of that and this. <br /><br />Looking for the Girl- The main character buys a dirty magazine in his youth and immortalizes the girl spread between the pages. He devotes his life to finding her, becoming a photographer, selling off all of his worldly possessions, and buying all of the magazines (of which she appears at different intervals in his life- the same and in age, but with a different name). <br /><br />Only the End of the World Again- Read this substanceless story for its language (it has a Scooby-Doo-ish plot).<br /><br />Bay Wolf- Fighting something from the Deep! Narrated in pulp “and then I ripped his arm off” fashion. <br /><br />We Can Get Them For You Wholesale- Brilliant first 3 pages! A man searches through a phone book for an assassin to kill the man who’s cheating with his girlfriend. <br /><br />Cold Colors- Crazy cool Dealing with computers and computer lingo, software, hardware mixed between metaphors. My favorite part was pigeon selling- people would buy them and spread their blood around their computer.<br /><br />The Sweeper of Dreams- T’was a nice short; think the ending was a “I have to end this and… meh.”<br /><br />Vampire Sestina- A vampire poem. The word blood is used. Ironically, the word suck is not.<br /><br />Mouse- What’s happening takes place in one paragraph near the end of the story. Everything else is exposition to that idea.<br /><br />Tastings- It’s sexually explitious! An erotic tale with a twist into supernatural fiction. Very well written.<br /><br />Babycakes- A story about eating babies… (sweet)<br /><br />Murder Mysteries- I waded through 292 pages to read this story!<br /><br />Snow, Glass, Apples- …I like the idea of holding her heart on the wall above the bed. <br /><br />(The short stories not mentioned are partiularly: MEH!)</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="1078891377189758968">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <a href="/user/show/28351026-tally" class="user" title="Tally">Tally</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/16790.Smoke_and_Mirrors" title="Paperback 9780380789023" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/28351026-tally?shelf=fantasy" class="actionLinkLite">fantasy</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/28351026-tally?shelf=short-stories" class="actionLinkLite">short-stories</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer916456772">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10058055139818352948">Short stories are like ice cream cones: they can be perfectly savored in one sitting. These ones in particular were deliciously entertaining. <br /><br />I have always loved Neil Gaiman's style (he is my favorite author, after all), and this collection is no different. It's an eclectic mix of oddities, wonders, spine-tinglers, and fairy tales turned upside down. Highly recommended, especially if you're in the mood for something short and sweet.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_1243971429">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1243971429" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/16796020-matt-garcia" class="left imgcol" title="Matt Garcia"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1381614904p2/16796020.jpg" alt="Matt Garcia" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/1243971429?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Apr 05, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/16796020-matt-garcia" class="user" title="Matt Garcia">Matt Garcia</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/16790.Smoke_and_Mirrors" title="Paperback 9780380789023" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1243971429">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3924062900263759959">Interesting collection with a wide variety of stories. Horror, fantasy, science fiction, and other genres are present in this collection. Gaiman's imagination is unique and some of his stories have the ability to grab you and not let go until the end. A crisp, clean writing style and inventive premises make this an enjoyable collection. Some stories are exemplary while others fell flat. Overall, a worthwhile read from a truly talented writer who is not bound to any sort of genre limitation.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

      <a href="/user/show/7008067-evans-light" class="user" title="Evans Light">Evans Light</a>

          is currently reading it


          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/16790.Smoke_and_Mirrors" title="Paperback 9780380789023" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/7008067-evans-light?shelf=have-it" class="actionLinkLite">have-it</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1330415444">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16457090501758598432">REVIEW WILL BE UPDATED PERIODICALLY AS I PROGRESS THROUGH THE BOOK.<br /><br />Much like Joe Hill did with the story hidden in the afterward of his 20th CENTURY GHOSTS collection, Gaiman has embedded a short tale, THE WEDDING PRESENT, in the introduction. It's well told, but doesn't ultimately lead to much. After this, his notes on all the tales in the book follow. While I truly enjoy author's notes in short story collections, I much prefer them to come after each story. <br /><br />CHIVALRY<br /><br />An old woman finds the Holy</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText16457090501758598432">REVIEW WILL BE UPDATED PERIODICALLY AS I PROGRESS THROUGH THE BOOK.<br /><br />Much like Joe Hill did with the story hidden in the afterward of his 20th CENTURY GHOSTS collection, Gaiman has embedded a short tale, THE WEDDING PRESENT, in the introduction. It's well told, but doesn't ultimately lead to much. After this, his notes on all the tales in the book follow. While I truly enjoy author's notes in short story collections, I much prefer them to come after each story. <br /><br />CHIVALRY<br /><br />An old woman finds the Holy Grail at a thrift store.<br />While this story was pleasantly told and had a somewhat-amusing concept, I can't label it as much more than a trifle.</span>

      <a href="/user/show/8850418-edward-lorn" class="user" title="Edward Lorn">Edward Lorn</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok">it was ok</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/1358538.Smoke_and_Mirrors" title="Paperback 9780061450167" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/8850418-edward-lorn?shelf=52-in-52-2014" class="actionLinkLite">52-in-52-2014</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer913465072">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10875188492586342463">SMOKE AND MIRRORS Review, or My Final Review For a While I'm a Neil Gaiman fanboy. I've loved all of his novels and a great deal of his short fiction, but this collection was marred with either lackluster outings or poems I couldn't enjoy because I personally don't understand what makes them poems. The latter is my own fault, and I do not hold it against the author. The former, on the other hand, is all Gaiman's fault. Many of these stories lack purpose, are nothing more than words compiled into</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText10875188492586342463">SMOKE AND MIRRORS Review, or My Final Review For a While I'm a Neil Gaiman fanboy. I've loved all of his novels and a great deal of his short fiction, but this collection was marred with either lackluster outings or poems I couldn't enjoy because I personally don't understand what makes them poems. The latter is my own fault, and I do not hold it against the author. The former, on the other hand, is all Gaiman's fault. Many of these stories lack purpose, are nothing more than words compiled into sentences and paragraphs. I can dig tales that have no definitive ending, or open endings, as it were, but when a piece of fiction has no reason whatsoever I fail to understand how or why it made it to print. Gaiman goes into great detail about how each of the stories in this collection came to be, and I can't help but wonder if the editors who requested a number of these stories only paid for them because they'd asked Gaiman for something and he delivered. Then, said editors felt responsible, perhaps thinking, "Well, we did ask for... something, and he did deliver." The biggest culprit here being the first outing, "Chivalry", wherein nothing happens other than a knight decked out in full armor (in modern times, mind you) trying time and time again to procure the holy grail from a stubborn old woman. In the end, Good Knight Galaad gets his grail and the reader's left wondering exactly what the hell was the story's purpose? There's no conflict, no tension, no drama, no twist, and not even a hint of climax. "Chivalry" accomplished nothing aside from making me slam my forehead into my desk in an attempt to knock the banality of the tale from my conscious mind. I think that, had I read SMOKE AND MIRRORS instead of listening to the audio book, I would have disliked far more of these stories than I did. Gaiman brought a certain whimsical panache to lesser tales, making them a great deal more interesting (e.g. "Troll Bridge", "Shoggoth's Old Peculiar" and "We Can Get Them for You Wholesale"). I think this came from knowing how the author felt the dialogue and prose should be read in order to get the most from the verbiage.<br /> <br />The stories that made me want to stick ice picks in my ears were: "Chivalry", "Don't Ask Jack", "The Daughter of Owls", and "One Life, Furnished in Early Moorcock". I didn't simply dislike these stories, I downright loathed them. Even Gaiman's narration seemed dull, as if he were apologizing for their existence by phoning in his performance. <br /> <br />The tales that stood out are as follows: "The Price", "Troll Bridge", "The Goldfish Pool and Other Stories", "Changes", "Shoggoth's Old Peculiar" (which didn't have a purpose either, but was enjoyable nonetheless because of the odd characters), "Only the End of the World Again". "Bay Wolf", "We can Get Them for You Wholesale", and "Mouse". Basically, half the collection was worth my time. Everything else was either meaningless or downright boring. Still, not a single entry in SMOKE AND MIRRORS matched the brilliance of his novels. I was hoping for short stroies on par with CORALINE or THE OCEAN AT THE END OF THE LANE or AMERICAN GODS. Sadly, I was disappointed. <br /> <br />All other stories not mentioned above were wholly unmentionable or entirely forgettable. Meaning, I couldn't even be bothered to complain about them.<br /> <br />In summation: If you're looking for a collection packed with amazing short stories, you can do far better than this. SMOKE AND MIRRORS is not the worst short story collection I've read, but it comes close. When Gaiman is on, he's terrific and magical and wonderfully creative, but when he's bad, sweet baby Tom Cruise, he'll make you want to castrate him with a rusty battleaxe then boil the dismembered bits in a vat of acid. Still, this grouping of fiction is well written. Even the worst of these tales are readable, which cannot be said for every short story author. Instead of this, I recommend ANANSI BOYS, THE GRAVEYARD BOOK, AMERICAN GODS, CORALINE (and, no, it's not only a children's book), THE OCEAN AT THE END OF THE LANE, or any of Gaiman's other novels. I highly recommend his series of SANDMAN comics, if you can get your hands on them, that is. If you would like a better collection from a different author, try BOOKS OF BLOOD, by Clive Barker (in my opinion, Barker is much better at short fiction than he'll ever be as a novelist), SKELETON CREW, by Stephen King, and any collection by Ray Bradbury.<br /> <br />2.5 out of 5 severely disappointed stars. (If you're reading this on Goodreads, I've rounded up to three.)</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="10875188492586342463">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer26016897">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16471421864280689080">Having read <a title="M is for Magic" href="https://www.goodreads.com/search/search?q=M%20is%20for%20Magic">M is for Magic</a> and <a title="Fragile Things" href="https://www.goodreads.com/search/search?q=Fragile%20Things">Fragile Things</a> I have encountered some of the short stories that Mr. Gaiman has written. I found this collection to be one of the most eclectic. Happy stories, sad stories, chilling stories, and erotic stories, but as he introduces them - all a product of smoke and mirrors. We're not to believe any of this, as it is all just an illusion. So why do I walk away feeling like it was all a bit too real?<br /><br />I enjoyed the very experimental feel to this book. Some prose, some</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText16471421864280689080">Having read <a title="M is for Magic" href="https://www.goodreads.com/search/search?q=M%20is%20for%20Magic">M is for Magic</a> and <a title="Fragile Things" href="https://www.goodreads.com/search/search?q=Fragile%20Things">Fragile Things</a> I have encountered some of the short stories that Mr. Gaiman has written. I found this collection to be one of the most eclectic. Happy stories, sad stories, chilling stories, and erotic stories, but as he introduces them - all a product of smoke and mirrors. We're not to believe any of this, as it is all just an illusion. So why do I walk away feeling like it was all a bit too real?<br /><br />I enjoyed the very experimental feel to this book. Some prose, some poetry. I found it a pleasure to read, and I appreciated the notes regarding each story and how it came to be. <br /><br />Flipping through the book now, it's hard to pick a favorite. I loved the charm of Chivalry. We Can Get Them For You Wholesale was a chilling thriller. I did not want Murder Mysteries to end. The White Road I long to hear recited over a campfire. Babycakes made me retch. Virus brought questions of the path that biotech is taking up. Snow, Glass, Apples... I dare say that I am unlikely to read the original with the same eyes again. <br /><br />It's a book worthy of many reads. </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer6156574359733936329">Very happy I read these. This is a collection of very adult Neil Gaiman stories, written before he fell into his trusty formula of "Ordinary guy meets strange person, and then enters wacky wonderful fantasy world." They're sad, sexy, naughty, shivery, eerie, and occasionally moving. There's an early story called "One Life, Furnished in Early Moorcock" that took my breath away, mainly because it must have been based on his own childhood. "Troll Bridge," a heart-tightening tale about the pain of g</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText6156574359733936329">Very happy I read these. This is a collection of very adult Neil Gaiman stories, written before he fell into his trusty formula of "Ordinary guy meets strange person, and then enters wacky wonderful fantasy world." They're sad, sexy, naughty, shivery, eerie, and occasionally moving. There's an early story called "One Life, Furnished in Early Moorcock" that took my breath away, mainly because it must have been based on his own childhood. "Troll Bridge," a heart-tightening tale about the pain of growing up and old and empty. "Changes," a warning about the perils of modern medicine. These days, Neil seems to bury his truth under gossamer layers of magic. In these stories, you will find bits and pieces of the real Neil. </span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="6156574359733936329">...more</a>

<span id="freeTextContainer2630175703152046130">"Stories are, in on way or another, mirrors. Fantasy-and all fiction is fantasy of one kind or another-is a mirror. A distorting mirror, to be sure, and a concealing mirror, set at 45 degrees to reality, but it's a mirror nonetheless, which we can use to tell ourselves things we might not otherwise see." <br /><br />As always anot</span>

Fantasy-and all fiction is fantasy of one kind or another-is a mirror. A distorting mirror, to be sure, and a concealing mirror, set at 45 degrees to reality, but it's a mirror nonetheless, which we can use to tell ourselves things we might not otherwise see." <br /><br />As always another wonderful book by Neil Gaiman. A great collection of short stories and poems that are haunting, disturbing, and funny all at the same time in a way that only Neil Gaiman can deliver. </span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_142925877">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/142925877" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/4107783-paul-pezski-perry" class="left imgcol" title="Paul 'Pezski' Perry"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1304357210p2/4107783.jpg" alt="Paul 'Pezski' Perry" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/142925877?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">May 14, 2011</a>

      <a href="/user/show/4107783-paul-pezski-perry" class="user" title="Paul 'Pezski' Perry">Paul 'Pezski' Perry</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/597623.Smoke_and_Mirrors" title="Paperback 9780755322831" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/4107783-paul-pezski-perry?shelf=fantasy" class="actionLinkLite">fantasy</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/4107783-paul-pezski-perry?shelf=horror" class="actionLinkLite">horror</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/4107783-paul-pezski-perry?shelf=myth" class="actionLinkLite">myth</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/4107783-paul-pezski-perry?shelf=short-stories" class="actionLinkLite">short-stories</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/4107783-paul-pezski-perry?shelf=fiction" class="actionLinkLite">fiction</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/4107783-paul-pezski-perry?shelf=mythology" class="actionLinkLite">mythology</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/4107783-paul-pezski-perry?shelf=read-in-2011" class="actionLinkLite">read-in-2011</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/4107783-paul-pezski-perry?shelf=male-author" class="actionLinkLite">male-author</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer142925877">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2393737058217668870">As with most short story collections, Gaiman's Smoke and Mirrors is something of a mixed bag. When he is good he is sublime, and there is plenty in this volume that fits that description, but there are also a few stories that seem little more than jottings of ideas meant to be fleshed out or perhaps left over from longer works. There is also some laudable inventiveness which, for me, doesn't always quite work - for example his triptych of narrative poems - but nonetheless shows the writer's grea</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText2393737058217668870">As with most short story collections, Gaiman's Smoke and Mirrors is something of a mixed bag. When he is good he is sublime, and there is plenty in this volume that fits that description, but there are also a few stories that seem little more than jottings of ideas meant to be fleshed out or perhaps left over from longer works. There is also some laudable inventiveness which, for me, doesn't always quite work - for example his triptych of narrative poems - but nonetheless shows the writer's great talent and shows also how important it is to stretch oneself.<br /><br />As I say, there are some utterly wonderful stories in this collection. The book closes with two of the best. <em>Murder Mysteries</em>, about the death of an angel during the construction of the universe and <em>Snow, Glass, Apples</em>, a new view on the Snow White story that is both reminiscent of Angela Carter and one of the best of its kind I have read. These and other stand-out stories such as <em>The Goldfish Pool and other stories</em> show, like Angela Carter, a deep connection to and understanding of myth and folklore - both an encyclopedic knowledge of the subject but also a thorough understanding of the workings and themes of the mythic, something that resonates through all his best work, from the Sandman graphic novels to <a title="American Gods by Neil Gaiman" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/4407.American_Gods">American Gods</a> and <a title="Stardust by Neil Gaiman" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/16793.Stardust">Stardust</a>.</span>

          </span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_1420367679">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1420367679" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/1188122-ben-babcock" class="left imgcol" title="Ben Babcock"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1211839871p2/1188122.jpg" alt="Ben Babcock" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/1420367679?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Oct 22, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/1188122-ben-babcock" class="user" title="Ben Babcock">Ben Babcock</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/1358538.Smoke_and_Mirrors" title="Paperback 9780061450167" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/1188122-ben-babcock?shelf=own" class="actionLinkLite">own</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/1188122-ben-babcock?shelf=fantasy" class="actionLinkLite">fantasy</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/1188122-ben-babcock?shelf=anthologies" class="actionLinkLite">anthologies</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/1188122-ben-babcock?shelf=2015-read" class="actionLinkLite">2015-read</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1420367679">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8405134446240524955">Now that I own copies of Neil Gaiman’s three short story anthologies, I re-read <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/181674343"> <em>Fragile Things</em> </a> and then tackled this one, <em>Smoke and Mirrors</em>. As with <em>Fragile Things</em> this earlier collection has a description of each story’s origin in the introduction. Unlike the other collection, <em>Smoke and Mirrors</em>’ introduction also comes with <strong>a bonus short story embedded</strong>. So, yeah. There’s that.<br /><br />I have to say that the more I read Gaiman’s stories the less unexpected or surprising they seem, if you know what I me</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText8405134446240524955">Now that I own copies of Neil Gaiman’s three short story anthologies, I re-read <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/181674343">
  <em>Fragile Things</em>
</a> and then tackled this one, <em>Smoke and Mirrors</em>. As with <em>Fragile Things</em> this earlier collection has a description of each story’s origin in the introduction. Unlike the other collection, <em>Smoke and Mirrors</em>’ introduction also comes with <strong>a bonus short story embedded</strong>. So, yeah. There’s that.<br /><br />I have to say that the more I read Gaiman’s stories the less unexpected or surprising they seem, if you know what I mean. Gaiman is a writer who loves to play with and subvert tropes, but he does it in very obvious ways. When there are twists, you can often see them coming. <em>Smoke and Mirrors</em> is rife with examples like this: “Snow, Glass, Apples” reimagines Snow White as a vampire child and the Queen as a heroine protecting her realm—it all ends poorly for her, still. There’s a story about a troll who wants to “eat the life” of a victim, which essentially means … well, I’ll let you guess.<br /><br />This unsurprising quality is not bad, just different. I’ve always appreciated Gaiman on a stylistic level. In particular, he often writes protagonists who are—or at least start off as—vaguely unsympathetic. I was never much a fan of Richard Mayhew from <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/524584581">
  <em>Neverwhere</em>
</a>, and many of the characters in these stories share that quality of being a less-than-stellar human being. It’s as if Gaiman is trying to say something….<br /><br />My favourite story is, by far, “We Can Get Them For You Wholesale,” and I’ll tell you why: I thought this was a Harlan Ellison story.<br /><br />I read this story a long time ago somewhere else—I don’t recall where now. I want to say it was in Grade 12, because that’s when I read a big anthology of Harlan Ellison’s works, but maybe I’m only claiming it was then because I was under the impression, for the longest time, that this story was written by Ellison. All I could remember was the premise: guy tries to take out a contract killing, but he gets up-sold by the marketing person until they agree to … well, I’ll let you guess. This is another example of where the twist is not so much surprising as almost stupefying in its logical progression, but I feel like it’s a very satisfying story.<br /><br />Anyway, for the longest time I’ve been going around telling people that one of my favourite short stories is this one by Ellison, not remembering what it was called. Turns out it’s actually by Neil Gaiman. So it goes.<br /><br />So for entirely personal reasons, “We Can Get Them For You Wholesale” is my favourite (and it is a very good story besides). The stories collected herein are all pretty good, actually. Some are so short it’s hard to really enjoy them—they are like a small candy you put in your mouth that melts just as it starts to release its flavour. “Chivalry,” the modern-day spoof on the quest for the Holy Grail, is a fantastic opener. I loved Gaiman’s characterization of Mrs Whitaker; she reminded me a lot of the types of older women I would meet in England or see on television there. “Murder Mysteries” reminds me a lot of <em>Supernatural</em>.<br /><br />But if it weren’t for that personal anecdote, then the best story of the collection has to be “The Price.” This story is heart-breaking. It’s about a heroic Black Cat fighting the forces of evil in a very visceral way, and I love every word of it. It’s simply and starkly written but powerful in the images it evokes and a reminder of the bond we have with our animals.<br /><br />I’ll echo the opinion I shared at the end of my review of <em>Fragile Things</em>: this is not where I would start with Gaiman. Encountering one of these stories alone in the wild might be compelling; so many all together like this feels too artificial. That’s the trouble with short story collections, isn’t it? Short stories are meant to be appreciated and savoured by themselves, but keeping them separately is inefficient and impractical. Collecting them takes them out of context, and reading such a collection robs them of some of their spontaneity.<br /><br />Be that as it may, <em>Smoke and Mirrors</em> is another good Gaiman read. It’s an excellent example of what he does best, which is take the familiar and look at it from a different perspective. In his introduction he says that all fiction is ultimately a form of fantasy. He’s not the first to make this observation, but I feel like he’s one writer in particular who takes such an observation to heart. A lot of Gaiman’s fantastic stories are set in a world like ours—a world where strange things happen, but unlike in this one, the people there get a little more idea of what’s going on. As if that’s ever a good idea.<br /><br /><a rel="nofollow" href="http://creativecommons.org/licenses/by-nc/4.0/">
  <img width="88" height="31" class="escapedImg" src="http://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1388723110i/7909581.png" alt="Creative Commons BY-NC License" /></a></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="8405134446240524955">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_1050132215">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1050132215" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/33114788-alexis-drake" class="left imgcol" title="Alexis Drake"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1405523305p2/33114788.jpg" alt="Alexis Drake" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/1050132215?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jul 31, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/33114788-alexis-drake" class="user" title="Alexis Drake">Alexis Drake</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/21277829-smoke-and-mirrors" title="Paperback " class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/33114788-alexis-drake?shelf=gaiman" class="actionLinkLite">gaiman</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1050132215">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17407824722479377797">3,75/5<br /> Chi mi segue già da un po’ sa che uno dei mei autori preferiti è Neil Gaiman, quindi, quando l’anno scorso sono stata in vacanza in Irlanda e Londra, ho colto l’occasione per prendere qualche suo volume in lingua originale, tra cui questo, Smoke and Mirrors, che è poi una raccolta di racconti.<br />Come un po’ tutte le raccolte di racconti, di qualsiasi autore, chiaramente ci sono dei racconti molto belli ed alcuni piuttosto insignificanti, o come in questo caso, abbastanza strampalati (cioè pi</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText17407824722479377797">3,75/5<br /> Chi mi segue già da un po’ sa che uno dei mei autori preferiti è Neil Gaiman, quindi, quando l’anno scorso sono stata in vacanza in Irlanda e Londra, ho colto l’occasione per prendere qualche suo volume in lingua originale, tra cui questo, Smoke and Mirrors, che è poi una raccolta di racconti.<br />Come un po’ tutte le raccolte di racconti, di qualsiasi autore, chiaramente ci sono dei racconti molto belli ed alcuni piuttosto insignificanti, o come in questo caso, abbastanza strampalati (cioè più strampalati di quello a cui Gaiman ci ha abituati) e piuttosto ostici da leggere.<br />Una delle cose che apprezzo maggiormente di queste raccolte, come era successo in Cose fragili, è l’introduzione, in cui l’autore spiega come, quando e perché ha scritto tutti i racconti del libro. A volte è una sezione un po’ lunga, ma è comunque molto interessante.<br />In questo caso, i racconti che mi sono piaciuti di più sono il primo “Chivalry”, poi “Troll Bridge”, “The goldfish pool and other stories” “How do you think it feels?” e gli ultimi due “Murder Mysteries” e “Snow, glass, apples”.<br />Chivalry è stupendo, è davvero in pieno stile Gaiman: una signora anziana trova in un mercatino dell’usato il Santo Graal, e per pochi spiccioli se lo porta a casa.<br />In seguito alla sua porta busserà qualcuno che desidera la coppa.<br />Ben scritto, fuori dagli schemi e sorprendente, l’ho adorato.<br />Troll bridge ricorda un po’ una favola dark irlandese, con un troll nascosto sotto un ponte che vuole mangiarsi le persone.<br />The goldfish pool è ambientato a Los Angeles, dove va uno scrittore perché Hollywood vuole trarre un film dal suo libro. Mi è piaciuto perché racconta il dietro le quinte di questo giro di affari, e come mai forse molto spesso i film tratti dai libri ricordino molto poco l’originale. Credo che sia piuttosto autobiografico anche.<br />How do you think it feels? Racconta dell’amore, tradito, corrisposto, clandestino, e di un uomo che soffre per amore e che desidera non provare più alcun sentimento nella sua vita.<br />Murder Mysteries invece è ambientato nelle strade buie e malfamate di una metropoli, dove un barbone chiede una sigaretta ad un uomo e in cambio gli racconta una storia: di come lui fosse l’angelo della vendetta del Signore e abbia risolto il caso di un angelo morto in paradiso durante la creazione. Suggestivo e particolare, mi è piaciuto molto.<br />Snow, glass, apples, come si evince dal titolo, è una sorta di retelling della fiaba di Biancaneve. Mi ha ricordato in una minima parte la storia di Regina di Once Upon a Time, ma questo retelling è molto più dark, più sanguinolento e drammatico. Ben fatto però, l’ho apprezzato.<br />Come dicevo però, non tutti i racconti sono a questi livelli, e molti sono davvero piuttosto spinti e con dettagli osè, quindi non è una lettura per tutti, anche perché il livello di inglese non è tra i più facili. Alcuni racconti sono comparsi già in altre raccolte, ma comunque, se siete fan di Gaiman, vi suggerisco di leggerlo, perché ci si addentra in un labirinto di specchi che danno su mondi fantastici ma anche pericolosi.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="17407824722479377797">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

              <a href="/review/list/9384958-kei-ci-bautista?shelf=my-books" class="actionLinkLite">my-books</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer326627458">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17994871960844862874">I have to say, in quite an unconventional manner, that this book is a house. It is a house of dark fantasy every child has ever subconsciously dreamed of while asleep, in one way or another. It could be me, but I think that most readers, had they been given a chance to read any one of the story in this book, would be fascinated and awed as to how Gaiman came up with such a story/stories. Some would think, 'how absurd,' but at the end of the day, at some virtual point, half the consideration it w</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText17994871960844862874">I have to say, in quite an unconventional manner, that this book is a house. It is a house of dark fantasy every child has ever subconsciously dreamed of while asleep, in one way or another. It could be me, but I think that most readers, had they been given a chance to read any one of the story in this book, would be fascinated and awed as to how Gaiman came up with such a story/stories. Some would think, 'how absurd,' but at the end of the day, at some virtual point, half the consideration it would require to realize, that it somehow hit an imagination. An idea. And every one of the story can have a different thread.<br /><br />I particularly liked 'Babycakes.' I have read it far too many times that sometimes I fear I might wake up from a bad dream 'cos as much as I wanted how it was told, my curiosity I'm afraid is not sufficient enough to want to see its image in motion.<br /><br />I would also like to applaud 'Murder Mysteries," for its highly engaging content, "Snow, Glass and Apples," cos I can never see Snow White the same way ever again, and "We Can Get Them For You WholeSale," which blew my mind.<br /><br />This collection is proof of Neil Gaiman's effective writing.<br /><br />Not all writers/story-tellers are quite effective, in a manner of speaking. But if you want a sudden escape from reality with all the frustrating stuff in this world, with some value-added twist, then this is the book for you.</span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_30821284">
