<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_950972902">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/950972902" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/5640151-tin" class="left imgcol" title="Tin"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1339924487p2/5640151.jpg" alt="Tin" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/950972902?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Feb 09, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/5640151-tin" class="user" title="Tin">Tin</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/16790.Smoke_and_Mirrors" title="Paperback 9780380789023" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/5640151-tin?shelf=favorites" class="actionLinkLite">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer950972902">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13488230225687503421">Smoke and Mirrors is a delightful collection of short stories and poems that are retellings of fairy tales and folklore of old. Reading it made me feel like a kid again, seeing a magic trick for the first time, and there is no grander magician than Neil Gaiman. He turns stock stories into new ones, more bewitching, more chilling and more surreal that it’s derivative. We get a mixture of horror, suspense, fantasy, and science fiction. What’s even better is that they all go beyond pure entertainme</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText13488230225687503421">Smoke and Mirrors is a delightful collection of short stories and poems that are retellings of fairy tales and folklore of old. Reading it made me feel like a kid again, seeing a magic trick for the first time, and there is no grander magician than Neil Gaiman. He turns stock stories into new ones, more bewitching, more chilling and more surreal that it’s derivative. We get a mixture of horror, suspense, fantasy, and science fiction. What’s even better is that they all go beyond pure entertainment because they reflect (like mirrors) a human condition or a state of the world, whether past, present or future. It has stories about technology, sex, Aids, medical drug development, life in Hollywood, the birth and end of the world. There are those stories that cast new light on vampires, werewolves, Santa Claus, Snow White and The Evil Queen. <br /><br />I feel like I have too many favorites. And I am only going to cover a few at length. Here they are:<br /><br />1. Murder Mysteries - This is a story about the angel Raguel, also called The Vengeance of God, tasked to solve the mysterious death of an angel from Silver City. I love how haunting and suspenseful this story is. It touches on the good and evil, birth and fall, love and jealousy. It also lives up to it's title. Right until the very end, I still found the whole story as enigmatic as when I started it.<br /><br />2. Snow, Glass, Apples - Pop culture is steeped in quite a number of Snow White retellings. And just when I thought I've seen and heard them all, in comes Gaiman. He's take on it is pretty darned unique and fantastic. He did some reverse engineering where The Evil Queen becomes the protagonist and Snow White is no longer our sweet, innocent princess. It is just deliciously dark. Probably like that poison apple. :)<br /><br />3. The Goldfish Pool and Other Stories- This one is about an author who comes to Hollywood in order to pen the script for a movie adaptation of his book. I took a liking to this because it reminds me a bit of the Coen Brothers' Barton Fink, and because I love movies. It's a bit of a biting commentary on Hollywood's commercialism. But what I loved about it is how it tackled memory. Here's a particular quote I loved. <em>"He says they (goldfish) only got a memory that’s like thirty seconds long. So they swim around the pool, it’s always a surprise to them, going ‘I never been here before.’ They meet another fish they known for a hundred years, they say, ‘Who are you, stranger?"</em><br /><br />4. We can Get them for you Wholesale - Because we all love a good bargain, and in the midst of one, can't seem to remember that Latin phrase: "caveat emptor."<br /><br />Then there's Troll Bridge and Only the End of the World Again, and so many more really. I think this may just be my favorite Neil Gaiman book to date.<br /><br />See original post here: <a rel="nofollow" href="http://rabbitin.blogspot.com/2014/08/smoke-and-mirrors-by-neil-gaiman.html">Rabbitin</a></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="13488230225687503421">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_142482865">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/142482865" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/4848495-airiz-c" class="left imgcol" title="Airiz C"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1420337239p2/4848495.jpg" alt="Airiz C" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/142482865?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jun 09, 2011</a>

      <a href="/user/show/4848495-airiz-c" class="user" title="Airiz C">Airiz C</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/16790.Smoke_and_Mirrors" title="Paperback 9780380789023" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/4848495-airiz-c?shelf=fantasy" class="actionLinkLite">fantasy</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/4848495-airiz-c?shelf=surreal" class="actionLinkLite">surreal</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/4848495-airiz-c?shelf=horror" class="actionLinkLite">horror</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/4848495-airiz-c?shelf=humor" class="actionLinkLite">humor</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/4848495-airiz-c?shelf=my-favorites" class="actionLinkLite">my-favorites</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/4848495-airiz-c?shelf=drama" class="actionLinkLite">drama</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/4848495-airiz-c?shelf=romance" class="actionLinkLite">romance</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/4848495-airiz-c?shelf=science-fiction" class="actionLinkLite">science-fiction</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/4848495-airiz-c?shelf=dark-humor" class="actionLinkLite">dark-humor</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer142482865">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8550643315981719083">Sir Terry Pratchett once said that Neil Gaiman is more of a conjurer than a wizard: “Wizards don’t have to work. They wave their hands, and the magic happens. But conjurers…work very hard. They spend a lot of time in their youth watching, very carefully, the conjurers of their day…and they take center stage and amaze you with flags of all nations and smoke and mirrors, and you cry, ‘Amazing! How does he do it? What happened to the elephant? Where’s the rabbit? Did he really smash my watch?’ And</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText8550643315981719083">Sir Terry Pratchett once said that Neil Gaiman is more of a conjurer than a wizard: “Wizards don’t have to work. They wave their hands, and the magic happens. But conjurers…work very hard. They spend a lot of time in their youth watching, very carefully, the conjurers of their day…and they take center stage and amaze you with flags of all nations and smoke and mirrors, and you cry, ‘Amazing! How does he do it? What happened to the elephant? Where’s the rabbit? Did he really smash my watch?’ And in the back row we, the other conjurers, say quietly, ‘Well done. Isn’t that a variant of the Prague Levitating Sock? Wasn’t that Pascual’s Spirit Mirror, where the girl isn’t really there? But where the hell did that flaming sword come from?’ And we wonder if there may be such a thing as wizardry after all…”<br />That pretty much sums up all my thoughts about Gaiman when I was reading Smoke and Mirrors, my first prose-and-poem anthology by my personal literary rock star.<br /><br />I’m enamored with his longer works like American Gods, Good Omens, and The Sandman series. Traipsing deeper into his fictional world, I found out that his shorter works are not a different beast entirely. The entries in Smoke and Mirrors maintain the same magic that his longer works have, in a way that the works cast a spell among the readers to continue reading.<br /><br /> You can tell that I’m a Gaimaniac, but that doesn’t mean I’m going to have this compilation overhyped. While this compendium still received two thumbs up from me, I must say that this is not the best representative of his genius. There are stories that are worth reading, but there are also some duds. <br />The stories I liked the most include: The Wedding Present, a story about a newly-wed couple with a cool The Picture of Dorian Gray-esque twist; Chivalry, a funny story about an old woman who bought the Holy Grail from a secondhand thrift shop; the Daughter of Owls, a story told in style of 17th century writer and historian John Aubrey; Snow, Glass, and Apples, a morbid reimagining of the tale of Snow White from the perspective of the Queen (if you read this, I guarantee you that you won’t be able to see the original story the same way again); Tastings, a well-written flash fiction about rare psychic abilities that are only present during sexual intercourse; and Murder Mysteries, a fascinating hardboiled crime story focusing on the first grave transgression committed in Heaven.<br /><br />Over all it’s an amazing read. Most of Gaiman’s stories are morbidly flummoxing, sexually explicit, and hauntingly violent. Speculative fiction buffs might like this treasure box of literature, and anyone who wants to have a light reading or expecting jolly fantasy stories can do themselves a favor and stay away from this book. :D Still, I reiterate for readers who want to enter Gaiman’s world, this anthology is not the best entranceway. You might want to start with Neverwhere or Stardust. :D<br /></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="8550643315981719083">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <a href="/user/show/888773-alex" class="user" title="Alex">Alex</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Gaiman fans, people who like dark lit</span></div>

        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/888773-alex?shelf=fantasy" class="actionLinkLite">fantasy</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer26596893">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8483555995171595096">This is a collection of short stories/poems, mostly with a "it's not what it seems" type theme. Because it's a collection, it's always difficult to rate. Most of the stories rate a strong 5 stars, but a few were only so-so, which dropped the rating.<br /><br />Some of my favorite stories were "Murder Mysteries," "Snow, Glass, Apples," "Changes," "We Can Get Them for You Wholesale," and "The Sweeper of Dreams." Not necessarily in that order.<br /><br />The strengths tended to be amazing creativity and story telling. The</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText8483555995171595096">This is a collection of short stories/poems, mostly with a "it's not what it seems" type theme. Because it's a collection, it's always difficult to rate. Most of the stories rate a strong 5 stars, but a few were only so-so, which dropped the rating.<br /><br />Some of my favorite stories were "Murder Mysteries," "Snow, Glass, Apples," "Changes," "We Can Get Them for You Wholesale," and "The Sweeper of Dreams." Not necessarily in that order.<br /><br />The strengths tended to be amazing creativity and story telling. The creation of worlds and lives inside a few pages was well executed. And like the original purpose of stories, each one seemed to teach a lesson and tell the reader more about life and living.<br /><br />The weakness that some stories had worked as a strength for some of the stories. I found some stories to be too vague, but this was only my first read through and subsequent reads (or more thorough reads) may reveal clearer understanding. <br /><br />This feels like a book I'll return to time and again, to flip through and read those stories that I hold dear and to re-discover those that I hadn't fully met. </span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_531795145">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/531795145" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/5448792-brendon-schrodinger" class="left imgcol" title="Brendon Schrodinger"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1392261804p2/5448792.jpg" alt="Brendon Schrodinger" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/531795145?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Feb 17, 2013</a>

      <a href="/user/show/5448792-brendon-schrodinger" class="user" title="Brendon Schrodinger">Brendon Schrodinger</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/597623.Smoke_and_Mirrors" title="Paperback 9780755322831" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/5448792-brendon-schrodinger?shelf=fantasy" class="actionLinkLite">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer531795145">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer641237702022232063">I have always been a bit of a Gaiman fan, ever since discovering <em>Sandman</em> and <em>American Gods</em> in the late nineties. However, I'm not such a huge enough fan to go and devour all his works at once. I don't think I do that with any authors. Anyway, I have eventually worked my way around to this collection. <br /><br />My partner and I have, for the second time, given eachother annual reading lists. These comprise of 5 books that the other must read in 2013. I guess the aim is to stir things up in our reading habi</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText641237702022232063">I have always been a bit of a Gaiman fan, ever since discovering <em>Sandman</em> and <em>American Gods</em> in the late nineties. However, I'm not such a huge enough fan to go and devour all his works at once. I don't think I do that with any authors. Anyway, I have eventually worked my way around to this collection. <br /><br />My partner and I have, for the second time, given eachother annual reading lists. These comprise of 5 books that the other must read in 2013. I guess the aim is to stir things up in our reading habits a little. <em>Smoke and Mirrors</em> was on her list for me to read. She is a bigger fan of Gaiman than I and I guess she was sick of this volume sitting on my shelf unread.<br /><br />I guess I was a little disappointed in the quality of these stories. I would have assumed to have been giving this collection a 4 star rating, but the amount of 2 star stories in the volume formed the majority. This majority seemed to be all Lovecraftian homages that lead nowhere and seemed to have no point.<br /><br />The few stand out stories were great. These include: "We Can Get Them For You Wholesale", "Looking for the Girl", "One Life, Furnished in Early Moorcock" and "Murder Mysteries" which I have previously read as the graphic novel version. <br /><br />You can see the same themes here as in his later books, but you can also see the need to be clever (which fails), the use of cliched story endings ("Get out! All that time that old man was a ghost"), and just general generalities.<br /><br />Also verse! <strong>I don't read verse.</strong> Call me ignorant and pig-headed. If you read and enjoy verse you may want to add a star to the rating. There are at least 5 verse stories for you to enjoy (and me to skip).<br /><br />Recommended for Gaiman fans only. For all others stick to his masterworks such as Sandman, American Gods, The Graveyard Book, Coraline etc etc<br /><br /></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="641237702022232063">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked &amp;&amp; exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&amp;name=' + shelf_name + '&amp;a=' + action + '&amp;authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('7voRmHuZphywWMkIgRSAMa2VJKQAWESuZ+x6SxCLbNOLLi5LiUuy5jyAvbP/dWaD5GLnvUmFAwQN5X/Z3B6alg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&amp;book_id=' + book_id + '&amp;refresh=true' + '&amp;authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('eEbznxPpSt3b1ja7OGUuRNsPR2dOtXagzqBLJ5jRbgsdksxM4TteJ1cOQgBGBMj2kviEfgdoMQqkqU61VESYTg==')})

This proves just one of several benign but inexplicable phenomena that begin to pull apart the family newly moved into the house as surely as a more sinister supernatural influence might. The title story beautifully captures the unpredictable potential of teenage lives through its account of a group of adolescent schoolfriends whose experiences subtly parallel events in a surreal TV fantasy series. Zombies serve as the focus for a young man\'s anxieties about his future in &amp;quot;Some Zombie Contingency Plans&amp;quot; and offer suggestive counterpoint to the lives of two convenience store clerks who serve them in &amp;quot;The Hortlak.&amp;quot; Not only does Link find fresh perspectives from which to explore familiar premises, she also forges ingenious connections between disparate       <div class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/work/quotes/6277491-smoke-and-mirrors-short-fiction-and-illusions">Quotes from Smoke and Mirrors</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div tyle="padding-bottom:15px" class="stacked">
            <span class="readable">“When I was a child, adults would tell me not to make things up, warning me of what would happen if I did. As far as I can tell so far, it seems to involve lots of foreign travel and not having to get up too early in the morning.”</span>
            <nobr>
              —
              <a href="/quotes/907-when-i-was-a-child-adults-would-tell-me-not" class="actionLinkLite">2992 likes</a>
            </nobr>
            <div class="clear"></div>
          </div>
          <div tyle="padding-bottom:15px" class="stacked">
            <span class="readable">“Memory is the great deceiver. Perhaps there are some individuals whose memories act like tape recordings, daily records of their lives complete in every detail, but I am not one of them. My memory is a patchwork of occurrences, of discontinuous events roughly sewn together: The parts I remember, I remember precisely, whilst other sections seemed to have vanished completely.”</span>
            <nobr>
              —
              <a href="/quotes/199565-memory-is-the-great-deceiver-perhaps-there-are-some-individuals" class="actionLinkLite">139 likes</a>
            </nobr>
            <div class="clear"></div>
          </div>
        <a href="/work/quotes/6277491-smoke-and-mirrors-short-fiction-and-illusions" style="float: right" class="actionLink">More quotes…</a>
